{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01RXuiN7du6BtsPwAP3jvtdb","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I see the issue! Look at the error handling:\n\nLine 1185-1186:\n```c\nif (error)\n    goto out_bad;\n```\n\nThis treats ANY error from the lookup as a reason to mark the dentry as invalid (out_bad returns 0).\n\nBut there's an out_error path (line 1236-1244) that returns the error code directly. The out_error is used for memory allocation failures (lines 1172-1180), not for RPC errors.\n\nThe problem is that when the lookup RPC call returns -ERESTARTSYS (because of a signal), it should NOT go to out_bad (which marks the dentry invalid). Now I understand the semantics. From namei.c:\n\nLine 1361-1369:\n```c\nif (unlikely(error <= 0)) {\n    if (error < 0) {\n        dput(dentry);\n        return ERR_PTR(error);  // Return error, let caller retry\n    } else {\n        d_invalidate(dentry);   // error == 0, invalidate the dentry\n        dput(dentry);\n        dentry = NULL;\n    }\n}\n```\n\nSo:\n- error > 0 (like 1): dentry is valid\n- error == 0: dentry is invalid, will try again later\n- error < 0: error, return error to caller\n\nThe issue is that nfs_lookup_revalidate returns 0 for ERESTARTSYS, which causes the dentry to be invalidated. Instead, it should return the error code (ERESTARTSYS) so the caller can handle it appropriately.Looking at line 1498-1505:\n```c\nif (unlikely(status <= 0)) {\n    if (status < 0) {\n        dput(dentry);\n        return status;  // Return error to caller\n    }\n    d_invalidate(dentry);  // status == 0, invalidate\n    dput(dentry);\n    goto need_lookup;\n}\n```\n\nSo when an error code is returned from d_revalidate, the VFS just returns it to the caller. If it's ERESTARTSYS, the caller (likely a system call) will handle it and retry.The fix is clear now:\n1. In nfs_lookup_revalidate, when the lookup RPC returns an error, check if it's a transient error like ERESTARTSYS\n2. If it is, return the error code instead of going to out_bad\n3. This is passed through to the NFS code.\n\nNow I'm confident about my analysis:\n\n**Root Cause:**\nThe nfs_lookup_revalidate function in fs/nfs/dir.c treats all errors from RPC calls (including ERESTARTSYS) as permanent failures that invalidate the dentry. This causes the dentry to be dropped, which can unmount the entire mount if the dentry is /storage itself or its parent.\n\n**Buggy Code:**\n1. Line 1158-1161: if (nfs_lookup_verify_inode(...)) { goto out_zap_parent; } - doesn't check if error is ERESTARTSYS\n2. Line 1183-1186: if (error) { goto out_bad; } - doesn't check if error is ERESTARTSYS\n\n**Fix:**\nCheck if the error is ERESTARTSYS or EINTR, and if so, return the error code to allow the VFS to retry, instead of marking the dentry as invalid.\n\nActually, let me double-check something. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01YGLmMKnEf2mSr4EV8C6iFU","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"text","text":"## Fault Localization Complete ✓\n\nI have successfully identified the fault in the Linux kernel NFS subsystem that causes autofs mounts to disappear. Here's my analysis:\n\n### **Buggy File & Function**\n- **File:** `fs/nfs/dir.c`\n- **Function:** `nfs_lookup_revalidate` \n\n### **Root Cause**\n\nThe bug occurs in how `nfs_lookup_revalidate` handles RPC errors, specifically signal-interrupted calls that return `ERESTARTSYS` (error code -512):\n\n1. **Location 1 (Lines 1158-1161):** When `nfs_lookup_verify_inode()` returns an error (which internally calls `__nfs_revalidate_inode` that performs a getattr RPC), any non-zero return value—including transient signal interruptions (`ERESTARTSYS`)—causes the code to go to `out_zap_parent` which invalidates the directory cache.\n\n2. **Location 2 (Lines 1183-1186):** When the lookup RPC call returns an error, including `ERESTARTSYS`, the code treats it as a permanent failure and goes to `out_bad`.\n\n3. **Final Result:** Both paths converge at `out_bad` (line 1235) which returns `0` (meaning \"dentry is invalid\"), causing the VFS to drop the dentry from the cache.\n\n### **Why This Is a Bug**\n\n`ERESTARTSYS` is **not** a permanent failure—it signals that an RPC was interrupted by a fatal signal and should be retried. However, the current code treats it like a permanent failure:\n- Invalidates the directory cache\n- Marks the inode as needing revalidation  \n- Drops the dentry\n\nWhen the dentry represents the autofs mount point `/storage` itself, dropping it unmounts the entire filesystem, even though the error was temporary.\n\n### **Impact**\n\nThis regression explains why:\n- The bug works in 3.14.12 (older RPC signal handling)\n- Fails in 4.1.15 (RPC can now return `ERESTARTSYS` directly)\n- Happens especially on first autofs mount expiration/unmount\n- tcpdump shows the server replied correctly (RPC was just interrupted on the client side)\n\nThe fix should distinguish between transient errors (`ERESTARTSYS`, `EINTR`) and permanent failures (`ESTALE`, etc.), returning the error code for transient failures instead of invalidating the dentry.\n\nResult saved to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json` ✓"}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":0,"cache_creation_input_tokens":868,"cache_read_input_tokens":58055,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":868},"output_tokens":5,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"e0898096-6858-46e2-827c-32cad7ad9f97","uuid":"e9176e8f-7b2c-47d6-ae61-de28788dfc73"}
